           be ever prepared to say, Come Lord Jesus, come quickly. Amen."
          01. Deter from sin
              i. Romans 14:10: "You, then, why do you judge your brother? Or
                 why do you look down on your brother? For we will all stand
                 before God's judgment seat."
             ii. 2 Corinthians 5:9-10: "So we make it our goal to please
                 him, whether we are at home in the body or away from it. 10
                 For we must all appear before the judgment seat of Christ,
                 that each one may receive what is due him for the things
                 done while in the body, whether good or bad."
            iii. Acts 17:30-31: "In the past God overlooked such ignorance,
                 but now he commands all people everywhere to repent. 31 For
                 he has set a day when he will judge the world with justice
                 by the man he has appointed. He has given proof of this to
                 all men by raising him from the dead."
          02. Consolation for the godly
              i. 2 Thessalonians 1:6-10: "God is just: He will pay back
                 trouble to those who trouble you 7 and give relief to you
                 who are troubled, and to us as well. This will happen when
                 the Lord Jesus is revealed from heaven in blazing fire with
                 his powerful angels. 8 He will punish those who do not know
                 God and do not obey the gospel of our Lord Jesus. 9 They
                 will be punished with everlasting destruction and shut out
                 from the presence of the Lord and from the majesty of his
                 power 10 on the day he comes to be glorified in his holy
                 people and to be marveled at among all those who have
                 believed. This includes you, because you believed our
                 testimony to you."


     8. When will Christ return? Defend your answer with Scripture proofs.
        a. WCF XXXIII.3: "...so will He have that day unknown to men, that
           they may shake off all carnal security, and be always watchful,
           because they know not at what hour the Lord will come; and may
           be ever prepared to say, Come Lord Jesus, come quickly. Amen."
          01. Unexpectedly
              i. Matthew 24:36, 42, 44: "No one knows about that day or
                 hour, not even the angels in heaven, nor the Son, but only
                 the Father...Therefore keep watch, because you do not know
                 on what day your Lord will come...So you also must be
                 ready, because the Son of Man will come at an hour when you
                 do not expect him."
             ii. 1 Thessalonians 5:1-3: "Now, brothers, about times and
                 dates we do not need to write to you, 2 for you know very
                 well that the day of the Lord will come like a thief in the
                 night. 3 While people are saying, "Peace and safety,"
                 destruction will come on them suddenly, as labor pains on a
                 pregnant woman, and they will not escape."
            iii. 2 Peter 3:9-10: "The Lord is not slow in keeping his
                 promise, as some understand slowness. He is patient with
                 you, not wanting anyone to perish, but everyone to come to
                 repentance. 10 But the day of the Lord will come like a
                 thief. The heavens will disappear with a roar; the elements
                 will be destroyed by fire, and the earth and everything in
                 it will be laid bare."
          02. Imminently
              i. Philippians 4:5: "Let your gentleness be evident to all.
                 The Lord is near."
             ii. James 5:8: "You too, be patient and stand firm, because the
                 Lord's coming is near."
            iii. Revelation 22:20: "He who testifies to these things says,
                 'Yes, I am coming soon.' Amen. Come, Lord Jesus."


        b. Return of the Man of Lawlessness
          01. 2 Thessalonians 2:1-12: "Concerning the coming of our Lord
              Jesus Christ and our being gathered to him, we ask you,
              brothers, 2 not to become easily unsettled or alarmed by some
              prophecy, report or letter supposed to have come from us,
              saying that the day of the Lord has already come. 3 Don't let
              anyone deceive you in any way, for that day will not come
              until the rebellion occurs and the man of lawlessness is
              revealed, the man doomed to destruction. 4 He will oppose and
              will exalt himself over everything that is called God or is
              worshiped, so that he sets himself up in God's temple,
              proclaiming himself to be God. 5 Don't you remember that when
              I was with you I used to tell you these things? 6 And now you
              know what is holding him back, so that he may be revealed at
              the proper time. 7 For the secret power of lawlessness is
              already at work; but the one who now holds it back will
              continue to do so till he is taken out of the way. 8 And then
              the lawless one will be revealed, whom the Lord Jesus will
              overthrow with the breath of his mouth and destroy by the
              splendor of his coming. 9 The coming of the lawless one will
              be in accordance with the work of Satan displayed in all
              kinds of counterfeit miracles, signs and wonders, 10 and in
              every sort of evil that deceives those who are perishing.
              They perish because they refused to love the truth and so be
              saved. 11 For this reason God sends them a powerful delusion
              so that they will believe the lie 12 and so that all will be
              condemned who have not believed the truth but have delighted
              in wickedness."


     9. What will heaven be like?
        a. From Peterson's Hell on Trial:
          01. City of God/Heavenly Marriage
              i. Revelation 21:3: "And I heard a loud voice from the throne
                 saying, 'Now the dwelling of God is with men, and he will
                 live with them. They will be his people, and God himself
                 will be with them and be their God.'"
          02. Joy
              i. Revelation 21:4: "He will wipe every tear from their eyes.
                 There will be no more death or mourning or crying or pain,
                 for the old order of things has passed away."
          03. Light
              i. Revelation 21:23: "The city does not need the sun or the
                 moon to shine on it, for the glory of God gives it light,
                 and the Lamb is its lamp."
          04. Family of God
              i. Revelation 21:7: "He who overcomes will inherit all this,
                 and I will be his God and he will be my son."
          05. Eternal Life
        b. The consummated kingdom will be a redeemed physical creation
          01. It is important to recognize that Revelation 21:2 depicts the
              new Jerusalem as descending to earth and Revelation 22:2
              takes us back to the garden of Eden with its mention of the
              tree of life and a river. Heavenly existence is not a
              disembodied existence but is a physical existence on a
              renewed heavens and earth. Moreover, Revelation 21:26, with
              its apparent allusion to Isaiah 60:5, may suggest that all
              that is good, culturally-speaking, in human society will
              persist into eternity.
              i. Jesus' resurrection body serves as a paradigm for us of the
                 redeemed creation.
                  . On the one hand, Jesus' resurrection body was clearly
                    different from his earthly body-e.g. at times Jesus was
                    not immediately recognized by those who knew him (Luke
                    24:30-31), and he was able to appear in rooms with
                    locked doors (John 20:19).
                  . Yet, on the other hand, Jesus' resurrection body was
                    also clearly continuous with his earthly body, and in
                    that sense, a real physical body-e.g. he ate to nourish
                    himself and the wounds from his crucifixion were still
                    recognizable (Luke 24:40-43). Thus all of creation, like
                    Jesus' resurrection body, will be both discontinuous
                    with and continuous with the present fallen creation.
          02. While biblical passages, like Romans 8:18ff. which pictures
              the personified fallen physical creation as an object of
              redemption, comport well with this interpretation of
              Revelation 21:1-22:5, other passages seem to imply either
              that heaven will be a spiritual existence away from the earth
              or that the present earth will be destroyed, in the sense of
              annihilated.
              i. 1 Thessalonians 4:17 seems to suggest that at the coming of
                 the Lord we will leave the earth to meet him in the air to
                 live a heavenly, not earthly, existence. Yet, the Greek
                 word translated "to meet" is a technical term that was used
                 in Hellenistic times for when a delegation of a city went
                 out to meet an incoming dignitary for the purpose of
                 escorting him back to the city. Thus Paul use of this term
                 in 1 Thessalonians 4:17 far from suggesting a heavenly
                 spiritual existence, instead implies that the Lord will be
                 escorted back to earth by his newly raised people to reign
                 on a redeemed physical creation.[93]
             ii. Due to the Left Behind series it might be thought that
                 Matthew 24:37-44 teaches that when the Lord returns he will
                 take his people with him to a heavenly existence and
                 destroy those who are left behind, so to speak. Yet, this
                 text compares the coming of the Lord with the flood in
                 Noah's day which swept away the wicked in judgment and left
                 behind righteous Noah and his family. Thus this text,
                 contrary to its popular interpretation, actually implies
                 that it is God's people who will be left behind.
            iii. On first glance 2 Peter 3:2-13 seems to conflict with this
                 interpretation in teaching that the present world will be
                 destroyed on the Day of Lord. As verse 10 says, the coming
                 Day of the Lord, "will bring about the destruction of the
                 heavens by fire, and the elements will melt in the heat."
                 However, upon closer inspection, this passage also teaches
                 of a future redeemed physical creation. This text
                 distinguishes between three worlds: a world before the
                 flood (v. 16); the present world between the flood and the
                 Day of the Lord (v. 7); and a future world after the Day of
                 the Lord, namely the new heavens and earth (v. 13). These
                 three worlds are the same world in three different periods
                 and are marked off from one another by the cosmic crises of
                 judgment by water and judgment by fire. This is important
                 because the world before the flood is spoken of as being
                 "destroyed" in verse 6 and yet it was not really destroyed
                 entirely but cleansed. So too the "destruction" facing the
                 present world will not annihilate it entirely but will
                 purify it of the sin that plagues it. This interpretation
                 is confirmed by the underlying Greek vocabulary of this
                 text which evokes the image of metallurgic purification in
                 the refiner's fire rather than annihilation.[94]


    10. Is there a hell? Defend your answer with Scripture proofs.
        a. Yes.
          01. Matthew 13:40-42: "As the weeds are pulled up and burned in
              the fire, so it will be at the end of the age. 41 The Son of
              Man will send out his angels, and they will weed out of his
              kingdom everything that causes sin and all who do evil. 42
              They will throw them into the fiery furnace, where there will
              be weeping and gnashing of teeth."
          02. Matthew 18:8-9: "If your hand or your foot causes you to sin
              cut it off and throw it away. It is better for you to enter
              life maimed or crippled than to have two hands or two feet
              and be thrown into eternal fire. 9 And if your eye causes you
              to sin, gouge it out and throw it away. It is better for you
              to enter life with one eye than to have two eyes and be
              thrown into the fire of hell."
          03. Mark 9:47-48: "And if your eye causes you to sin, pluck it
              out. It is better for you to enter the kingdom of God with
              one eye than to have two eyes and be thrown into hell, 48
              where 'their worm does not die, and the fire is not
              quenched.'"
          04. 2 Thessalonians 1:9: "They will be punished with everlasting
              destruction and shut out from the presence of the Lord and
              from the majesty of his power...."


    11. What is "annihilationism?" Evaluate it biblically.
        a. Annihilationism is the view that unbelievers are annihilated
           rather than suffer eternal conscious torment.
        b. Peterson answers five common arguments from annihilationists:
           the arguments based on the vocabulary of destruction, hell-fire
           imagery, God's justice, universalist passages, and conditional
           immortality.
          01. Vocabulary of Destruction
              i. On response involves the observation that the Beast, the
                 False Prophet, and Satan will be cast into the fire and
                 John says (Rev 20:10) that they "will be tormented day and
                 night for ever and ever."
             ii. Peterson also observes that the biblical imagery used to
                 speak of hell (darkness and separation, fire, "weeping and
                 gnashing of teeth," punishment, and death and destruction)
                 only at times can appear to support annihilationism.
                 However, when the whole of the biblical picture is
                 observed, annihilationism is not an option.
          02. Hell-fire Imagery:
              i. Peterson responds that hell-fire speaks of the pain of the
                 wicked, not of their consumption.
          03. God's Justice:
              i. On page 173 Peterson says, "We must learn of divine justice
                 from the Bible itself. It will not do to protest God's
                 revealed judgments on the basis of what seems fair or
                 unfair to us. Instead, we must adjust our thinking,
                 including our view of God's justice, to revealed truth."
             ii. Thomas Aquinas: "Further, the magnitude of the punishment
                 matches the magnitude of the sin...Now a sin that is
                 against God is infinite; the higher the person against whom
                 it is committed, the graver the sin-it is more criminal to
                 strike a head of state than a private citizen-and God is of
                 infinite greatness. Therefore an infinite punishment is
                 deserved for a sin committed against him."
          04. Universalist Passages:
              i. Universalists and annihilationists have to argue that the
                 last three chapters of the Bible are not a picture of the
                 final state for these chapters reject both views.
          05. Conditional Immortality:
              i. The parallelism in Matthew 25:46 ("Then they will go away
                 to eternal punishment, but the righteous to eternal life.")
                 suggests that just as eternal life is continued existence,
                 so too is eternal punishment.


    12. What is your view of the millennium? Briefly defend your view from
        Scripture.
        a. I am amillennial.
          01. Basic Principles
              i. The NT must be allowed to interpret the Old
             ii. The OT prophets spoke of the glories of the Messianic Age
                 to come in terms of the types and figures of their own age:
                 the people of Israel, the land of Palestine, the city of
                 Jerusalem, the temple, the sacrifices, the throne of David.
            iii. We are to interpret such figures in light of the NT
                 revelation of their significance:
                  . Israel: The church is the new Israel (e.g. Phil 3:2-3)
                  . Palestine: Palestine symbolizes the renewed earth (Mat
                    5:5; Eph 6:1-3)
                  . Jerusalem: Jerusalem will descend from heaven (Rev 21)
                  . Throne of David: Jesus reigns upon it (Luke 1:30-33)
                  . Temple: Jesus is greater than the temple (Mat 12:6) and
                    we are the temple corporately (1 Cor 3:16; Eph 2:19-22)
                    and individually (1 Cor 6:19-20)
        b. Revelation 20
          01. The binding of Satan and the final battle correspond to two
              climaxes in battle against Satan by Christ, namely the cross
              and second coming. The dragon, or ancient serpent (cf. Gen
              3), is bound. This recapitulates Revelation 12 where the
              dragon can't harm the church which flees into the desert. The
              binding is for the specific purpose of not being able to
              deceive the nations (cf. Christ's binding of the strong man
              in Mat 12:29; cf. also Jude 6 which portrays the fallen
              angels as bound in darkness).
          02. Hoekema: "We therefore understand the word ezesan (lived, or
              came to life) in verse 4 as describing the fact that the
              souls of believers who have died are now living with Christ
              in heaven and sharing in his reign during the intermediate
              state between death and resurrection. The thousand-year
              period during which these souls live and reign with Christ
              is, as we saw, the entire gospel era, from the first coming
              of Christ to the Second Coming. In other words, the
              millennium is now, and the reign of Christ with believers
              during this millennium is not an earthly but a heavenly
              one."[95]
          03. Premillennialists understand what is described in Revelation
              20:11-13 as the resurrection of unbelievers. However, this
              conflicts with John 5:28-29, which depicts a single
              resurrection of believers and unbelievers.
        c.   Romans 9-11: All Israel Will Be Saved?[96]
          01. "There is much difference of opinion among biblical scholars
              as to the meaning of the clause 'and so all Israel will be
              saved.' There are, in the main, three interpretations of the
              clause."
              i. "Many interpreters understand these words as meaning that
                 the nation of Israel as a totality (though not necessarily
                 every single member of that nation) will be converted after
                 the fulness of the Gentiles has been gathered into the
                 kingdom of God."
             ii. "A second interpretation of the clause 'and so all Israel
                 will be saved' understands it as referring to the salvation
                 of all the elect, not only from the Jews but also from the
                 Gentiles, throughout history."
            iii. "A third interpretation of the clause in question
                 understands it as describing the bring to salvation
                 throughout history of the total number of the elect from
                 among the Jews."
          02. "The interpretation of the words 'and so all Israel will be
              saved' which does most justice to the Scriptural givens is
              the third."
              i. "The problem which engages Paul in Romans 9-11 is the
                 thorny one of the unbelief of Israel...The question which
                 troubles him is expressed in its sharpest terms in Romans
                 11:1, 'I ask, then, has God rejected his people?'"
             ii. "In chapter 9 Paul makes the point that the apparent
                 rejection of Israel is not complete. Here the answer to his
                 question comes down to this: 'Not all who are descended
                 from Israel are Israel' (9:6, NIV). That is to say, though
                 it is true that many Israelites are lost, the true
                 Israelites are not lost but saved."
            iii. "In chapter 10 Paul goes on to show that the rejection of a
                 substantial portion of Israel is not arbitrary. Here he
                 further develops the point that the Israelites who are lost
                 are responsible for their own rejection of the gospel."
                  . "One verse in chapter 10 deserves special attention,
                    verse 12: 'For there is no distinction between Jew and
                    Greek; the same Lord is Lord of all and bestows his
                    riches upon all who call upon him.' Paul's point here is
                    that as far as the obtaining of salvation is concerned,
                    there is no distinction between Jew and Greek. If this
                    is so, a future period of time in which only Jews will
                    be saved, or in which Jews will be saved in a way which
                    is different from the way in which Greeks or Gentiles
                    are saved, would seem to be ruled out."
             iv. "In chapter 11 Paul demonstrates the rejection of Israel is
                 neither absolute nor unqualified."
                  . Hoekema's interpretation of 11:25-26a: "Though Israel
                    has been hardened in its unbelief, this hardening has
                    always been and will continue to be only a partial
                    hardening, never a total hardening. In other words,
                    Israel will continue to turn to the Lord until the
                    Parousia, while at the same time the fulness of the
                    Gentiles is being gathered in. And in this way all
                    Israel will be saved: not just the last generation of
                    Israelites, but all true Israelites-all those who are
                    not just of Israel but are Israel, to use the language
                    of Romans 9:6. Another way of putting this would be: all
                    Israel in Romans 11:26 means the totality of the elect
                    among Israel. The salvation of all Israel, therefore,
                    does not take place exclusively at the end-time, but
                    takes place throughout the era between Christ's first
                    and second coming-in fact, from the time of the call of
                    Abraham."
                  . "It should be added that the interpretation of Romans
                    11:26a just advanced does not exclude a possible large-
                    scale conversion of the Jews to Christianity in the
                    future, but leaves room for it. In fact, why should
                    there not be more than one such large-scale turning of
                    Jews to Christ in the future? There is nothing in the
                    passage which would rule out such a future conversion or
                    such future conversions, as long as one does not insist
                    that the passage points only to the future, or that it
                    describes a conversion of Israel which occurs after the
                    full number of Gentiles has been gathered in."



      2 Other Questions



    13. What does the Bible teach about the Holy Spirit's work in the Old
        Testament?[97]
        a. In essence, it appears that the Holy Spirit in the OT is the
           agent of giving life, revealing God's message, and enabling
           God's people. In particular, the Holy Spirit's work in the OT
           has to do with:
          01. Shaping creation (Gen 1:2; Psalm 33:6), animating animals and
              mankind (Gen 2:7; Job 33:4; Psalm 104:29-30; Isaiah 34:16),
              and directing nature and history.
          02. Revealing God's messages to his spokesmen (2 Sam 23:2; Neh
              9:30; Isaiah 61:1-4).
          03. Teaching the way to be faithful and fruitful (Neh 9:20; Psalm
              143:10; Isaiah 11:2).
          04. Eliciting faith, repentance, obedience, and righteousness
              (Psalm 51:10-12).
          05. Giving skill and application for creative work (Exodus 31:1-
              11).
        b. Ferguson: "In the New Testament's understanding of salvation,
           certain moral and spiritual characteristics are produced
           exclusively by the Spirit. But these (e.g. the fruit of the
           Spirit in Galatians 5:22-23) are already exemplified by Old
           Testament believers. Moreover, these believers are set before
           New Testament believers not only as examples of justification by
           faith (e.g. Heb. 11:1ff.; Jas. 2:14-26; 5:17-18) or of what it
           means to walk by the Spirit. Hence, Christian believers can turn
           to the Psalms not only to find their own experiences of sorrow,
           doubt, fear and even despair mirrored there, but, as is commonly
           confused, to find examples of wholehearted adoration and
           devotion that exemplify what it means to worship God by the
           Spirit. Such exhibitions of the presence of the saving fruit of
           the Spirit argue for the presence of his soteriological ministry
           in the old covenant...one of the temptations of a theology of
           the Spirit which recognizes the deep-rooted continuity of
           revelation in the Bible is so to stress the continuity of the
           Spirit's ministry that we are in danger of flattening the
           contours of redemptive history, and of undermining the genuine
           diversity and development from old to new covenants. Paul's
           teaching in 2 Corinthians 3 indicates that there is an epochal
           development from the old to the new, precisely in terms of the
           ministry of the Spirit."[98]


    14. What is the Holy Spirit's function today? Is it different than in
        the past?
        a. In the OT, the Holy Spirit pointed prophets to the coming
           sufferings and glories of the Messiah (1 Peter 1:10-13), whereas
           in the NT the Holy Spirit (John 14:25) inspired the
           inscripturated revelation and convicts of sin (John 16:8-11).
        b. While in the OT the Spirit indwelt believers, in the NT the
           Spirit indwells believers specifically as the Spirit of Exalted
           Christ.
          01. Regarding John 14:15-17, Ferguson says, "The contrast is
              located not in the manner of his dwelling so much as in the
              capacity in which he indwells. This giving of the Spirit thus
              announces the divine exaltation of Christ to the right hand
              of the Father...It is in this sense that John sees the
              difference that Pentecost signals in the ministry of the
              Spirit. Now, as the bond of union to God, the Spirit indwells
              all who believe as the Spirit of the Lord Jesus Christ. This
              is a development of epochal proportions."[99]


    15. What happened at Pentecost? How does this relate to the church
        today?
        a. "Pentecost publicly marks the transition from the old to the new
           covenant, and signifies the commencement of the 'now' of the day
           of salvation (2 Cor. 6:2). It is the threshold of the last days,
           and inaugurates the new era in which the eschatological life of
           the future invades the present evil age in a proleptic
           manner."[100]
        b. Relation to the Church Today:[101]
          01. Ethnic Universalism
              i. The Spirit "was now 'poured out' by Christ in unrestrained
                 measure, and distributed without geographical and ethnic
                 limitation, 'on all people.'"
             ii. Reversal of Babel.
          02. New Status/Relationship for God's People
              i. In light of Moses' wish in Numbers 11:29 that the Lord
                 would put his Spirit on all people, in the new covenant
                 "That which came to the people by and large through
                 official channels in the Mosaic economy (via prophets,
                 priests and kings) now belongs to all the Lord's people by
                 Christ through the Spirit. A status (prophet) and
                 relationship (intimate knowledge, cf. Am. 3:7) with God,
                 known at first hand only by the few under the old covenant,
                 could now be enjoyed by all."




    16. Distinguish between the gifts and the fruit of the Spirit.
        a. Gifts of the Spirit can be described as that which is essential
           in the building up of God's church. The fruit of the Spirit has
           to do with the personal transformation of character in the life
           of an individual believer. Examples of gifts of the Sprit can be
           found in Romans 12, 1 Corinthians 12-14, and Ephesians 4. The
           fruit of the Spirit is found in Galatians 5:22-23.


    17. Does the Spirit give gifts today? Explain.
        a. Yes. The passages describing the gifts clearly have validity
           today.


    18. Are there gifts mentioned in Scripture that are not given today?
        Explain and defend.
        a. No. However, I would argue that certain gifts are less prominent
           and only perhaps come to the fore in establishing the church in
           areas in which the gospel has hitherto been unknown or long
           forgotten, such as healings and tongues in known languages, etc.
           It is important to note that the exercise of gifts even in
           Apostolic times was not automatic since Paul left Trophimus sick
           in Miletus (2 Tim 4:20).


    19. What do New Testament passages teach us concerning the following
        work of the Holy Spirit?:


        a. How he comes
          01. As a dove upon Christ (Mat 3:16; Mark 1:10; Luke 3:22; John
              1:32)
          02. In Wind and Tongues of Fire (Acts 2:1-4).
          03. Through the hearing of the Word (Eph 1:13)
          04. Through the laying on of hands witnessed to by tongues and
              praise (e.g. Acts 19:1-7).


        b. What he does
          01. Reveals Jesus' reality and the truth about him by:
              i. Reminding and further instructing the apostles (John 14:26;
                 16:13; Eph 3:2-6)
             ii. Enlightening others to receive the apostolic witness (John
                 16:8-11; Acts 10:44-48).
          02. Unites believers to Christ in regenerative, life-giving co-
              resurrection so that they become sharers in his kingdom and
              members in the body (Rom 6:3-11; Eph 2:1-10; 4:3-16).
          03. Assures believers that they are children and heirs of God
              (Rom 8:12-17).
          04. Mediates the fellowship with the Father and the Son as a
              first installment of what is to come (Rom 8:23; 2 Cor 5:5;
              Eph 1:14).
          05. Transforms believers progressively through prayer and
              conflict with sin into Christ's moral and spiritual likeness
              (2 Cor 3:18).
          06. Enables spiritual gifts (Rom 12:3-8; 1 Cor 12; Eph 4).
          07. Prays effectively in and for believers in Christ who feel
              unable to pray for themselves (Rom 8:26-27).
          08. Prompts missionary action to make Christ known (Acts 8:29)
              and pastoral decision (Acts 15:28).


        c. How he works
          01. In our hearts by and with the Word (John 6:63).


        d. What his ministry is today
          01. Mediates "knowledge of, and union and communion with, the
              physically withdrawn, ascended, and glorified savior (Jn
              14:15-26; 16:14)."[102] Also convicts the world of sin (John
              6:8-11).
          02. Applies the benefits of redemption in terms of effectual
              calling, regeneration, and sanctification.


    20. How would you answer charismatic claims from Scripture?
           Follow the instructions in 1 Corinthians 12-14.


        Answer from the Scriptures:


        a. A Mormon
          01. Beliefs
              i. Mormon's believe, "As man is, God once was; and as God is,
                 man will become."
          02. Critique
              i. Historically, there is no evidence for the claims of
                 Mormonism regarding peoples who supposedly populated North
                 America.
             ii. Philosophically, this belief suffers from the problem of
                 infinite regress. If God was once a man ad infinitum,
                 whence creation?
            iii. Biblically, the following texts undermine such a view of
                 God:
                  . Psalm 90:2: "Before the mountains were born or you
                    brought forth the earth and the world, from everlasting
                    to everlasting you are God."
                  . John 1:1-2: "In the beginning was the Word, and the Word
                    was with God, and the Word was God. 2 He was with God in
                    the beginning."


        b. A Jehovah's Witness
          01. Beliefs
              i. JW's deny the Trinity, claim that Jesus is just one of many
                 gods and that Jesus returned secretly in the 20th century.
                  . In support of their view of divinity they cite John
                    10:34-36: "Jesus answered them, "Is it not written in
                    your Law, 'I have said you are gods?' 35 If he called
                    them 'gods,' to whom the word of God came-and the
                    Scripture cannot be broken- 36 what about the one whom
                    the Father set apart as his very own and sent into the
                    world? Why then do you accuse me of blasphemy because I
                    said, 'I am God's Son?'"




          02. Critique
              i. The Trinitarian formulas in Matthew 28:18-20 and 2
                 Corinthians 13:14 are very difficult to explain if the
                 Trinity is denied, not to mention the passages which
                 portray the Son and Spirit and divine.
             ii. John 1:1 is a predicate nominative and thus there is no
                 need for an article.
            iii. Jesus' second coming is going to be public (Mat 26:64). The
                 "thief in the night" metaphor refers not to hidden-ness but
                 to suddenness.
             iv. Regarding John 10:34-36, Jesus is quoting Psalm 82:6. Verse
                 7 goes on to mock the supposed divine status by pointing
                 out that they will die like mere men.
                  .  Psalm 82:6-7: "I said, 'You are 'gods'; you are all
                    sons of the Most High.' 7 But you will die like mere
                    men; you will fall like every other ruler."


   J. Sacraments (WCF 27-29; WLC 161-177; WSC 91-97)

   F. Study Questions on the History of the PCA
