        Morton H. Smith, W. Jack Williamson, Ken Keyes, and G. Aiken
        Taylor.
     6. What are some distinctives of the PCA?


   The Half-Way Covenant
   The Half-Way Covenant was a form of partial church membership created by
   New England Puritans in 1662. It was promoted in particular by the
   Reverend Solomon Stoddard. The Half-Way Covenant provided a partial
   church membership for the children and grandchildren of church members.
   Those who accepted the Covenant, and agreed to follow the creed and rules
   of the church, could become church members without claiming a spiritual
   experience. These half-members could not vote on any issues within the
   church, although all members could participate in the sacrament of the
   Supper.



   Study Questions on Church Government and Discipline



   Have you read the Book of Church Order of the Presbyterian Church in
   America?
   Are you aware of any of its principles about which you have reservations?
   Explain.


   (References are to chapters in the BCO.)


   G. Preface and Principles (Preface & Chapter 1)


     1. Who is the head of the church? How does he exercise his authority?


        a. Jesus Christ is the head of the church and contains in himself
           all the offices in his church. He rules and teaches the church
           through his Word and Spirit by the ministry of men, thus
           mediately exercising his own authority and enforcing his own
           laws unto the edification and establishment of his kingdom.


     2. List at least two key principles of Presbyterian church government.
        Can the church "bind" men's consciences? Why or why not?


        a. Key principles include:
          01. God alone is Lord of the conscience and has left it free from
              any doctrines/commandments of men which are contrary to the
              Word of God or which in regard to matters of faith and
              worship are not governed by the Word of God.
          02. Every church or communion of churches is entitled to declare
              the terms of admission into its communion and the
              qualifications of its ministers and members as well as the
              whole system of internal government which Christ has
              appointed (this derives from principle 01).
          03. Christ has appointed officers not only to preach the Gospel
              and administer the sacraments but also to exercise discipline
              for the preservation of both truth and duty.
          04. Godliness is founded on truth.
          05. All teachers must be sound in faith, though there are truths
              and forms with respect to which men of good character and
              principles may differ (relates to principle 04).
          06. The power to elect persons to the exercise of authority in
              any particular society resides in that society, though those
              elected and how they are elected must be in accordance with
              Scripture.
          07. Since the Holy Scriptures are the only rule of faith and
              practice, all church power is only ministerial and
              declarative. Thus no church judicatory may make laws to bind
              the conscience. Moreover, all church courts may err through
              human frailty.
          08. Ecclesiastical discipline is moral and spiritual and derives
              force only from its own justice, the approval an impartial
              public, and the blessing of Christ.


     3. What is the Constitution of the Presbyterian Church in America?


        a. The Constitution of the PCA, which is subordinate to the Holy
           Scriptures, consists of the doctrinal standards set forth in the
           Westminster Confession of Faith, together with the Larger and
           Shorter Catechisms, and the Book of Church Order, comprising the
           Form of Government, the Rules of Discipline, and the Directory
           for Worship; all as adopted by the Church.


   H. The Church and Its Members (Chapters 2-6)


     1. What is the visible church? Who are its members? (chapter 2)


        a. The Visible Church before the law, under the law, and now under
           the Gospel, is one and the same and consists of all those who
           make profession of their faith in the Lord Jesus Christ,
           together with their children.


     2. What is the power of the church? How does it differ from that of
        the state? (chapter 3)


        a. The power of the church is wholly spiritual and is twofold. It
           is exercised individually by officers in preaching the Gospel,
           administering the Sacraments, reproving the erring, visiting the
           sick, and comforting the afflicted. It is also exercised jointly
           in Church courts.



        |                                                               |
|Power of Church vs. Power of State                             |
|  |                            |                              |
|  |Church                      |State                         |
|  |                            |                              |
|1.|Spiritual power             |Power includes the exercise of|
|  |                            |force                         |
|  |                            |                              |
|2.|Constitution derives from   |Constitution must be          |
|  |divine revelation           |determined by human reason and|
|  |                            |the course of providential    |
|  |                            |events                        |
|  |                            |                              |
|3.|Church has no right to      |The State has no right to     |
|  |construct or modify State   |frame a creed or polity for   |
|  |government.                 |the church.                   |
|                                                               |
|The Church and the State are as planets moving in concentric   |
|orbits: "Render unto Caesar the things that are Caesar's and to|
|God the things that are God's" (Mat 22:21).                    |


     3. What is a particular church? (chapter 4)


        a. A particular church consists of a number of professing
           Christians, with their children, associated together for divine
           worship and godly living, agreeable to the Scriptures, and
           submitting to the lawful government of Christ's kingdom. Its
           officers are its teaching and ruling elders, and its deacons.
           Its jurisdiction, being a joint power, is lodged in the church
           Session, which consists of its pastor, pastors, associate
           pastor(s), and ruling elders.


     4. What is a mission church? (chapter 5)


        a. A mission church is distinguished from a particular church in
           that it has no permanent governing body and thus must be
           governed or supervised by others. However, its goal is to mature
           and be organized as a particular church as soon as this can be
           done decently and in good order.


     5. What two kinds of members does the church have? What are their
        respective rights and privileges? (chapter 6)


        a. A church consists of communing members and non-communing
           members.
          01. Communing members are those who have made a profession of
              faith in Christ, have been baptized, and have been admitted
              by the Session to the Lord's Table.
          02. Non-communing members are baptized children of communing
              members.
        b. All baptized persons are entitled to the watchful care,
           instruction and government of the church. However, only
           communing members can partake of communion and serve in church
           offices such as ruling elder and deacon.


   I. Church Officers (Chapters 7-9)


     1. What permanent officers has Christ given to his Church?


        a. Elders (including Teaching Elders and Ruling Elders) and
           deacons.


     2. What are the qualifications for an elder? What are his duties? How
        are ruling and teaching elders alike? How are they different? What
        is meant by the "parity" of ruling and teaching elders?


        a. Qualifications:
          01. Male
          02. Blameless life
          03. Sound in faith
          04. Apt to teach
          05. Sobriety and holiness of life becoming the Gospel
          06. Rules his own house well
          07. Has a good reputation among those outside the church


        b. Duties:
          01. As a bishop/pastor, he has oversight of the flock.
              i. E.g., watches over the flock to make sure not corruption of
                 doctrine or morals enters therein
          02. As a presbyter/elder it is his duty to be grave and prudent,
              an example to the flock, and to govern well in the house and
              Kingdom of Christ.
              i. E.g., visits the sick, prays
          03. As a teacher, he expounds the Word, and by sound doctrine
              both exhorts and convinces.
              i. E.g., instructs the ignorant, comforts mourners, nourishes
                 and guards children of the church, evangelizes with zeal


        c. Ruling vs. Teaching Elders:
          01. In addition to all of the responsibilities of the Ruling
              Elder, a Teaching Elder must feed the flock by reading,
              expounding, and preaching the Word of God and administering
              the Sacraments.
              i. As an ambassador, he is sent to declare the will of God to
                 sinners, and to beseech them to be reconciled to God
                 through Christ
             ii. As an evangelist, he bears glad tidings of salvation to the
                 ignorant and perishing
            iii. As a preacher, he stands to proclaim the Gospel
             iv. As a steward of the mysteries of God, he dispenses the
                 manifold grace of God and the ordinances instituted by
                 Christ
          02. Ruling elders are those with gifts and commission by Christ
              to govern


        d. Parity of Ruling and Teaching Elders:
          01. Elders being of one class of office, ruling elders possess
              the same authority and eligibility to office in the courts of
              the Church as teaching elders. They should, moreover,
              cultivate zealously their own aptness to teach the Bible and
              should improve every opportunity of doing so.

     3. What are the duties of deacons? What are the qualifications for
        deacons?


        a. General Duties:
          01. The office of deacon is one of sympathy and service, after
              the example of the Lord Jesus Christ; it also expresses the
              communion of the saints, especially in their helping one
              another in time of need.
        b. Specific Duties:
          01. Minister to those in need, to the sick, to the friendless,
              and to any who may be in distress.
          02. Develop the grace of liberality in the members of the church,
              to devise effective methods of collecting the gifts of the
              people, and to distribute these gifts among the objects to
              which they are contributed.
          03. They have care of the property of the congregation both real
              and personal and keep in proper repair the church edifice and
              other buildings belonging to the congregation.
              i. Though in matters of special importance affecting the
                 property of the church, they cannot take final action
                 without the approval of the Session and consent of the
                 congregation.


           Note:
                  . In the discharge of their duties the deacons are under
                    the supervision and authority of the Session.
                  . In a church in which it is impossible for any reason to
                    secure deacons, the duties of the office devolve upon
                    the ruling elders.


        c. Qualifications:
          01. Men
          02. Spiritual Character
          03. Honest repute
          04. Exemplary lives
          05. Brotherly spirit
          06. Warm sympathies
          07. Sound Judgment


   J. Church Courts (Chapters 10-15)


     1. Name the courts of the church. What is the proper or original
        jurisdiction of each? What officers must each court have? How are
        they chosen? (chapters 10-11)


        a. The courts of the church are Sessions, Presbyteries, and the
           General Assembly.
        b. Every court has the right to resolve questions of doctrine and
           discipline and in general to maintain truth and righteousness,
           and condemn erroneous opinions and practices. The Session
           exercises jurisdiction over a single church; the Presbytery over
           what is common to the ministers, Sessions, and churches within a
           prescribed district; and the General Assembly over such matters
           as concern the whole Church. The lower courts are subject to the
           higher ones.
        c. Each court must have a moderator and a clerk.
          01. A moderator has all authority necessary for the preservation
              of order and for the proper and expeditious conduct of all
              business before the court, and for convening and adjourning
              the court according to its own ruling as well as notifying
              others in sufficient advance of a necessary change in
              time/place of a meeting.
          02. A clerk records transactions, preserves the records
              carefully, and grants extracts from the records when needed.
        d. How Chosen:
          01. Choice of a Moderator:
              i. Session
                  . For prudential reasons the pastor is moderator of the
                    Session.
             ii. Presbytery
                  . The moderator of the Presbytery may be elected at each
                    stated meeting of the court, or, for a period of time up
                    to one year.
            iii. General Assembly
                  . The moderator of the General Assembly shall be chosen at
                    each stated meeting; he, or in case of his absence the
                    last moderator present or the oldest minister longest a
                    member of the court, shall open the next meeting with a
                    sermon unless it is impracticable, and shall hold the
                    chair until a new moderator be chosen.
          02. A clerk or clerks shall be elected by the Session,
              Presbytery, and General Assembly to serve for a definite
              period as determined by the court.


     2. Who are the members of the church session? What are the main duties
        of the session? (chapter 12)


        a. The church Session consists of the pastor, associate pastor(s),
           if there be any, and the ruling elders of a church [assistant
           pastor(s) are not members of the Session but may be invited to
           attend].
        b. The Session is charged with maintaining the spiritual government
           of the church, for which purpose it has power:
          01. Regarding Members
              i. Inquire into members' knowledge, principles, and conduct
             ii. Censure those found delinquent
            iii. See that parents present their children for baptism
             iv. Receive members into the communion of the Church
              v. Remove members for just cause
             vi. Grant letters of dismissal to other churches (including
                 names of members' non-communing baptized children)
          02. Regarding Officers and Budget
              i. Examine, ordain, and install ruling elders and deacons upon
                 their election
             ii. Require ruling elders and deacons to devote themselves to
                 their work
            iii. Examine the records of deacons
             iv. Approve and adopt the budget
          03. Regarding Property
              i. Approve actions of special importance affecting the
                 property
          04. General Duties
              i. Call congregational meetings as needed
             ii. Establish and control Sunday schools and Bible classes
            iii. Establish and control all special groups (e.g., men in the
                 church, women in the church, children's groups)
             iv. Promote World Missions
              v. Promote obedience to the Great Commission at home and
                 abroad
             vi. Order collections for pious uses
          05. Regarding Worship
              i. Exercise authority over
                  . Time and place of preaching and administering of
                    Sacraments
                  . All other religious services
                  . Uses of church buildings and associated properties
             ii. Take oversight of singing in public worship
            iii. Ensure Word is preached only by qualified men
             iv. Assemble people for worship when there is no minister
              v. Determine best measure to promote spiritual interests
          06. Regarding Higher Courts
              i. Observe and carry out lawful injunctions of higher courts
             ii. Appoint representative to higher courts who shall report
          07. Regarding Records
              i. Keep records of baptisms, communing members, non-communing
                 members, deaths and dismissals of church members


     3. Who are the members of presbytery? To what church does a minister
        belong? How is an ordained minister received into a presbytery? How
        is a church received into a presbytery? What are the main duties
        and responsibilities of the presbytery? (chapter 13)


        a. The members of presbytery are all teaching elders and churches
           within its bounds. When the presbytery meets, however, it
           consists of all teaching elders and duly elected ruling elders
           from the churches within its bounds.
        b. A minister shall be required to hold his membership in the
           Presbytery within whose geographical bounds he resides, unless
           there are reasons which are satisfactory to his Presbytery why
           he should not do so.
        c. Ordained ministers are received into a presbytery after being
           examined on Christian experience, their views on theology, the
           Sacraments, and church government.
        d. The Presbytery, before receiving into its membership any church,
           shall designate a commission to meet with the church's ruling
           elders to make certain that the elders understand and can
           sincerely adopt the doctrines and polity of the PCA as contained
           in its Constitution. In the presence of the commission, the
           ruling elders shall be required to answer affirmatively the
           questions required of officers at their ordination.
        e. The main duties and responsibilities of the presbytery are:
          01. Regarding Candidates and Ministers
              i. Candidates: to receive candidates under care, examine and
                 license them
             ii. Ministers: to receive, dismiss, ordain, install, remove,
                 and judge them
          02. Regarding Sessions
              i. Review their records
             ii. Redress their errors
            iii. Take care that they observe the Church's Constitution
          03. Regarding Pastoral Relations
              i. Establish and dissolve them
          04. Regarding Efforts of Evangelists and Ministers
              i. Evangelists: se them apart to proper work
             ii. Ministers: require diligence, censure delinquent
          05. Regarding Injunctions of Higher Courts
              i. See that they are obeyed
          06. Regarding Churches
              i. Condemn error injuring the Church's purity and peace
             ii. Visit churches to inquire and redress evils having arisen
            iii. Unite or divide churches as their members request
             iv. Form and receive new churches
              v. Take special oversight of churches without pastors
             vi. Dissolve churches
            vii. Dismiss churches with their consent
          07. General
              i. Devise measures to enlarge the Church within its bounds
             ii. Order whatever pertains to the spiritual welfare of the
                 churches under its care
          08. Regarding Proposals to General Assembly
              i. Propose to GA measures of common advantage to the Church at
                 large
          09. Regarding Records and Reports
              i. Keep full and accurate records of its proceedings and send
                 them to GA


     4. What are the main duties and responsibilities of the General
        Assembly? What are the permanent committees and agencies of the
        General Assembly? What is a committee of commissioners? How do a
        committee of commissioners and a permanent committee or agency
        differ? (chapter 14)


        a. Main duties/responsibilities:
          01. GA is responsible to encourage and promote the fulfillment of
              the Great Commission by the various courts
          02. Receive and issue all appeals, references and complaints
              brought from lower courts
          03. Bear testimony against error in doctrine and immorality in
              practice
          04. Decide all controversies respecting doctrine and discipline
          05. Give advice and instruction in conformity with the
              Constitution
          06. Review records of Presbyteries to make sure they follow the
              Constitution and to redress whatever they may have done
              contrary to order
          07. Devise measures for promoting the prosperity and enlargement
              of the Church
          08. Erect new Presbyteries and unite/divide those which were
              erected with their consent
          09. Institute and superintend the agencies necessary in the
              general work of evangelization and appoint ministers of such
              labors
          10. Suppress schismatical contentions and disputations
          11. Receive other bodies conforming to PCA doctrine and order,
              with consent of � of Presbyteries
          12. Authorize Presbyteries to receive bodies suited to become
              "constituents" of their courts and lying within its
              geographical bounds
          13. Correspond with other churches
          14. Unite (per BCO 26) with other ecclesiastical bodies
              conforming to PCA doctrine and order
          15. Recommend measures to promote charity, truth, and holiness


        b. The permanent committees and agencies of the General Assembly
           are:
          01. Administrative Committee of General Assembly
          02. Committee on Christian Education and Publications
          03. Committee on Mission to North America
          04. Committee on Mission to the World
          05. Committee on Reformed University Ministries


        c. ?


        d. ?

     5. What is the difference between a committee and a commission?
        (chapter 15)


        a. A commission differs from an ordinary committee in that while a
           committee is appointed to examine, consider, and report, a
           commission is authorized to deliberate upon and conclude the
           business referred to it, except in the case of judicial
           commissions of a Presbytery appointed under BCO 15-3 [Presbytery
           as a whole may try a judicial case within its jurisdiction].


   K. Church Orders (Chapters 16-24)


     1. How is a man called to office in the church? (chapter 16)


        a. Ordinary vocation to office in the Church is the calling of God
           by the Spirit, through the inward testimony of a good
           conscience, the manifest approbation of God's people, and the
           concurring judgment of a lawful court of the Church.


     2. What is a candidate? What is required to become a candidate?
        (chapter 18)


        a. A candidate for the ministry is a member of the Church in full
           communion who, believing himself to be called to preach the
           Gospel, submits himself to the care and guidance of the
           Presbytery in his course of study and of practical training to
           prepare himself for this office.
        b. Requirements for candidacy include:
          01. Endorsement of the candidates Session consisting of
              testimonials regarding his Christian character and promise of
              usefulness in ministry, with description and evaluation of
              activities in ministry.
          02. Must be a member of the congregation for at least six months,
              except in cases deemed extraordinary.
          03. Must file application with clerk of the Presbytery at least
              one month before the meeting of the Presbytery


     3. What is a licentiate? In what areas is a prospective licentiate
        examined? What is internship? (chapter 19)


        a. A licentiate is one who has been examined by the Presbytery and
           granted a license to preach the Gospel and thus can preach in
           PCA pulpits on a regular basis


        b. After giving a statement with regard to his Christian experience
           and inward call to preach the Gospel, a prospective licentiate
           is examined in the following areas:
          01. Basic knowledge of biblical doctrine as outlined in the
              Confession of Faith and Larger and Shorter Catechisms of the
              PCA
          02. Practical knowledge of the Bible's content
          03. Basic knowledge of the government of the PCA as defined in
              the BCO


        c. In accordance with the Scriptural requirement that some trial be
           previously made of those ordained to the ministry of the Word
           concerning gifts and abilities, a candidate for ordination must
           serve one year internship as a time of practical instruction and
           testing of the intern's gifts


     4. What steps must a church take in calling a pastor? (chapter 20)


        a. The steps are as follows:
          01. The Session shall call a congregational meeting to elect a
              pulpit committee which may be composed of members from the
              congregation at large or the Session, as designated by the
              congregation
          02. The pulpit committee shall, after consultation and
              deliberation, recommend to the congregation a pastoral
              candidate who, in its judgment, fulfills the Constitutional
              requirements of that office and is most suited to be
              profitable to the spiritual interests of the congregation
          03. The Session shall call a congregational meeting to convene at
              the regular place of worship, giving at least one week public
              notice of the time, place, and purpose of this meeting
          04. The Session shall appoint one of their number to call the
              meeting to order and to preside over it. All communing
              members in good and regular standing may vote.
          05. Election must be by a majority of voters. If a large minority
              of voters objects the moderator shall try to convince them to
              withdraw the call but if they refuse then the call shall
              proceed.
          06. One or more commissioners shall be appointed by the church to
              present and prosecute the call before their Presbytery.
          07. A proper call must be written in the hands of the Presbytery
              prior to being acted upon by the Presbytery, including
              financial arrangements (such as salary, vacation, insurance,
              retirement, etc.) between those calling and the one called
              and assurance that the definite work will afford the liberty
              to proclaim and practice fully and freely the whole counsel
              of God, as contained in the Scriptures and understood in the
              Westminster Confession of Faith.
          08. A pastor called from another presbytery must be examined by
              the one into which he is called and must be released for
              transfer by his present Presbytery
          09. A pastor must consent to the call


     5. In what areas must a candidate for ordination be examined? What
        vows must he take? (chapter 21)


        a. Areas for examination include:
          01. Acquaintance with experiential religion, personal character
              and family management
          02. Knowledge of Greek and Hebrew languages
          03. Bible content
          04. Theology
          05. Sacraments
          06. Church history
          07. History of PCA
          08. Principles and rules of the government and discipline of the
              church
          09. Theological thesis
          10. Exegetical paper, using original languages, on a passage of
              Scripture
          11. Preach a sermon before the Presbytery or a committee


        b. Vows include:
          01. Do you believe the Scriptures of the Old and New Testaments,
              as originally given, to be the inerrant Word of God, the only
              infallible rule of faith and practice?
          02. Do you sincerely receive and adopt the Confession of Faith
              and the Catechisms of this Church, as containing the system
              of doctrine taught in the Holy Scriptures; and do you further
              promise that if at any time you find yourself out of accord
              with any of the fundamentals of this system of doctrine, you
              will on your own initiative, make known to your Presbytery
              the change which has taken place in your views since the
              assumption of this ordination vow?
          03. Do you approve of the form of government and discipline of
              the Presbyterian Church in America, in conformity with the
              general principles of Biblical polity?
          04. Do you promise subjection to your brethren in the Lord?
          05. Have you been induced, as far as you know your own heart, to
              seek the office of the holy ministry from love to God and a
              sincere desire to promote His glory in the Gospel of His Son?
          06. Do you promise to be zealous and faithful in maintaining the
              truths of the Gospel and the purity and peace and unity of
              the Church, whatever persecution or opposition may arise unto
              you on that account?
          07. Do you engage to be faithful and diligent in the exercise of
              all your duties as a Christian and a minister of the Gospel,
              whether personal or relational, private or public; and to
              endeavor by the grace of God to adorn the profession of the
              Gospel in your manner of life, and to walk with exemplary
              piety before the flock of which God shall make you overseer?
          08. Are you now willing to take the charge of this church,
              agreeable to your declaration when accepting their call? And
              do you, relying upon God for strength, promise to discharge
              to it the duties of a pastor?


     6. Who has the final say in establishing or dissolving a pastoral
        relationship? How may a pastoral relation be dissolved? (chapters
        21, 23)


        a. The Presbytery has the final say in establishing and dissolving
           a pastoral relationship.
        b. The dissolution of a pastoral relation:
          01. Pastor initiated:
              i. The pastor shall tender the resignation of his pastoral
                 charge to his Presbytery, the Presbytery shall cite the
                 church to appear by its commissioners, to show cause why
                 the Presbytery should or should not accept the resignation.
                 If the church fails to appear, or if its reasons for
                 retaining its pastor be deemed insufficient, his
                 resignation shall be accepted and the pastoral relation
                 dissolved.
             ii. There shall always be a meeting of the congregation called
                 and conducted in the same manner as the call of the pastor.
          02. Church initiated:
              i. Same as above, except the church initiates.


     7. What is the difference between an associate pastor and an assistant
        pastor? (chapter 22)


        a. An associate pastor, like the pastor, is elected by the
           congregation and thus a member of the Session.
        b. An assistant pastor is called by the Session, by the permission
           and approval of Presbytery. He is not a member of the Session
           but may be appointed on special occasions to moderate the
           Session.
        c. Thus the relationship of the associate pastor to the church is
           determined by the congregation while the relationship of the
           assistant pastor to the church is determined by the Session. The
           dissolution of both is governed by the provision of BCO 23.


     8. What steps must be followed in electing ruling elders or deacons?
        In what areas is a nominee to be examined? (chapter 24)


        a. The steps for electing ruling elders/deacons are as follows:
          01. At such times as determined by the Session, communicant
              members of the congregation may submit names to the Session,
              keeping in mind that each prospective officer should be an
              active male member who meets the qualifications set forth in
              1 Timothy 3 and Titus 1.
          02. Nominees for the office of ruling elder/deacon shall receive
              instruction in the qualifications and work of the office.
          03. Each nominee shall be examined in:
              i. His Christian experience, especially his personal character
                 and family management (based on the qualifications set out
                 in 1 Timothy 3:1-7 and Titus 1:6-9)
             ii. His knowledge of the system of doctrine, government,
                 discipline contained in the Constitution of the PCA
            iii. The duties of the office to which he has been nominated
             iv. His willingness to give assent to the questions required
                 for ordination
          04. If there are candidates eligible for election, the Session
              shall report to the congregation those eligible, giving at
              least (30) days prior notice of the time and place of
              congregational meeting for elections.


   L. Congregational Meetings; Amending the Constitution (Chapters 25-26)


     1. How may a congregational meeting be called? Who can vote? What
        officers are required? Who owns the property of the local church?
        (chapter 25)


        a. How a congregational meeting may be called:
          01. The Session shall call a congregational meeting when it seems
              in the best interest of the church (no business shall be
              transacted except what is stated in the notice)
          02. The Session shall always call a congregational meeting when
              requested to do so by:
              i. 1/4th of communing members of a church of 100 members or
                 less
             ii. 1/5th of 101-300
            iii. 1/6th of 301-500
             iv. 1/7th of 501-700
              v. 100 members if 701 and above
          03. If the session fails to call a meeting within 30 days from
              the receipt of the request, then any member or members in
              good standing may file a complaint in accordance with the
              provisions of BCO 43
        b. All communing members in good standing may vote.
        c. The officers required are a moderator and clerk.
        d. All particular churches shall be entitled to hold, own and enjoy
           their own local properties, without any right of reversion
           whatsoever to any Presbytery, General Assembly or any other
           courts hereafter created, trustees or other officers of such
           courts.


     2. How may the Book of Church Order be amended? How may the doctrinal
        standards be amended? (chapter 26)


        a. Amendments to the BCO may be made only in the following manner:
          01. Approval of the proposed amendment by majority of those
              present and voting in the General Assembly, and its
              recommendation to the Presbyteries
          02. The advice and consent of two-thirds (2/3) of the
              Presbyteries
          03. The approval and enactment by a subsequent General Assembly
              by a majority of those present and voting


        b. The doctrinal standards, that is, the Confession of Faith and
           the Larger and Shorter Catechisms, may be amended only in the
           following manner:
          01. Approval of the proposed amendment by three-fourths (3/4) of
              those present and voting in the General Assembly, and its
              recommendation to the Presbyteries
          02. The advice and consent of three-fourths (3/4) of the
              Presbyteries
          03. The approval and enactment by a subsequent General Assembly
              by three-fourths (3/4) of those present and voting


   M. Principles of Discipline (Chapters 27-30)


     1. What is church discipline? What is the goal of church discipline?
        What are its proper steps? (chapter 27)


        a. Discipline is the exercise of authority given the Church by the
           Lord Jesus Christ to instruct and guide its members and to
           promote its purity and welfare. The term "discipline" has two
           senses:
          01. The one referring to the whole government, inspection,
              training, guardianship and control which the church maintains
              over its members, its officers and its courts
          02. The other a restricted and technical sense, signifying
              judicial process


        b. The goal of church discipline is:
          01. Rebuke of offenses
          02. Removal of scandal
          03. Vindication of the honor of Christ
          04. Promotion of purity and general edification of the Church
          05. Spiritual good of the offenders themselves


        c. The proper steps of church discipline are:
          01. Instruction in the Word
          02. Individual's responsibility to admonish one another (Mat
              18:15; Gal 6:1)
          03. If the admonition is rejected, then the calling of one or
              more witnesses (Mat 18:16)
          04. If rejection persists, then the Church must act through her
              court unto admonition, suspension, excommunication and
              deposition


     2. Who is primarily responsible for disciplining non-communing
        members? (chapter 28)


        a. The Session shall encourage the parents of the Church to guide
           their children in the catechizing and disciplining of them in
           the Christian religion. Thus the parents are primarily
           responsible for disciplining their children as non-communing
           members.






     3. List and define church censures (chapter 30)


        a. Censures by church courts include:
          01. Admonition
              i. Admonition is the formal reproof of an offender by a church
                 court, warning him of his guilt and danger, and exhorting
                 him to be more circumspect and watchful in the future.
          02. Suspension from the Sacraments
              i. Suspension from the Sacraments is the temporary exclusion
                 from those ordinances, and is indefinite as to its
                 duration. There is no definite suspension from the
                 Sacraments.
          03. Excommunication
              i. Excommunication is the excision of an offender from the
                 communion of the Church. This censure is to be inflicted
                 only on account of gross crime or heresy and when the
                 offender shows himself incorrigible and contumacious. The
                 design of this censure is to operate on the offender as a
                 means of reclaiming him, to deliver the church from the
                 scandal of his offense, and to inspire all with fear by the
                 example of his discipline.
          04. Suspension from office
              i. Suspension from office is the exclusion of a church officer
                 from his office. This may be definite or indefinite as to
                 its duration. With respect to church officers, suspension
                 from Sacraments shall always be accompanied by suspension
                 from office. But suspension from office is not always
                 necessarily accompanied with suspension from Sacraments.
             ii. Definite suspension from office is administered when the
                 credit of religion, the honor of Christ, and the good of
                 the delinquent demand it, even though the delinquent has
                 given satisfaction to the court.
            iii. Indefinite suspension is administered to the impenitent
                 offender until he exhibits signs of repentance, or until by
                 his conduct, the necessity of the greatest censure be made
                 manifest.
          05. Deposition from office
              i. Deposition is the degradation of an officer from his
                 office, and may or may not be accompanied with the
                 infliction of other censure.


   N. The Process of Discipline (Chapters 31-38)


     1. With what court should charges be filed? What must be done before
        formal charges are brought? When must a formal judicial process be
        pursued? (chapter 31)


        a. The filing of charges:
          01. In the case of a minister, original jurisdiction (the right
              first to hear and determine) shall be in the Presbytery of
              which the minister is a member, except in cases provided in
              BCO 34-1 [If the Presbytery refuses to act in doctrinal cases
              or cases of public scandal and two other Presbyteries request
              the General Assembly to assume original jurisdiction (to
              first receive and initially hear and determine), the General
              Assembly shall do so].
          02. In the case of church member, original jurisdiction belongs
              to the Session of church of which he/she is a member, except
              in cases provided in BCO 33-1 [If Session refuses to act in
              doctrinal cases or instances of public scandal and two other
              Sessions of churches in the same Presbytery request the
              Presbytery of which the church is a member to initiate proper
              or appropriate action in a case of process and thus assume
              jurisdiction and authority, the Presbytery shall do so].


        b. Before formal charges are brought:
          01. If a personal offense:
              i. The means of reconciliation and reclaiming the offender
                 required by Christ in Mat 18:15-16 shall be followed: "'If
                 your brother sins against you, go and show him his fault,
                 just between the two of you. If he listens to you, you have
                 won your brother over. 16 But if he will not listen, take
                 one or two others along, so that 'every matter may be
                 established by the testimony of two or three witnesses.'"
             ii. Caution must be exercised when entertaining an accusation
                 from a person known to have a malevolent sprit, etc.
          02. When the offense is general the case may be conducted either
              by any person appearing as prosecutor or by a prosecutor
              appointed by the court. There are many cases in which it will
              promote the interests of religion to send a committee to
              converse in a private manner with the offender to endeavor to
              bring him to a sense of guilt, before instituting the actual
              process.


        c. A formal judicial process must be pursued if there is a strong
           presumption of guilt. It is pursued by appointing a prosecutor
           to prepare the indictment and to conduct the case. The
           prosecutor shall be a member of the court, but if the case is
           before the Session, he may be any communing member of the same
           congregation with the accused. The accuser is always the PCA and
           the prosecutor represents the church.


     2. How many witnesses are required? (chapter 35)


        a. More than one witness is required, unless there is also
           corroborative evidence.


     3. How should a censure be administered? (chapter 36)


        a. For private offenses, censure should be administered in the
           presence of the court alone, or in private by one or more
           members of the court.
        b. In the case of public offenses, the degree of censure and mode
           of administering it shall be within the discretion of the court.
        c. The censure of admonition should be administered in private by
           one or more members of the court if the offense is known only to
           a few and is not aggravated in character.
        d. If the offense is public the admonition should be administered
           by the moderator in presence of the court and may also be
           announced in public should the court deem it expedient.


     4. What is the goal of discipline in regard to the offender? (chapter
        37)


        a. The goal of discipline in regard to the offender is repentance
           and restoration.


   O. Review and Control; Jurisdiction (Chapters 39-46)


     1. Define "review and control."


        a. It is the right and duty of every court above the Session to
           review, at least once a year, the records of the court next
           below, and if any lower court fails to present its records for
           this purpose, the higher court may require them to be produced
           immediately, or at any time fixed by this higher court.
        b. In reviewing records of a lower court the higher court is to
           examine:
          01. Whether the proceedings have been correctly recorded;
          02. Whether they have been regular and in accordance with the
              Constitution;
          03. Whether they have been wise, equitable and suited to promote
              the welfare of the Church;
          04. Whether the lawful injunctions of the higher court have been
              obeyed.


     2. Define "reference."


        a. A reference is a written representation and application made by
           a lower court to a higher for advice or other action on a matter
           pending before the lower court, and is ordinarily to be made to
           the next higher court.
        b. Among proper subjects for reference are matters that are new,
           delicate or difficult; or on which the members of the lower
           court are very seriously divided; or which relate to questions
           involving the Constitution and legal procedures respecting which
           the lower court feels the need of guidance.
        c. In making a reference the lower court may ask for advice only,
           or for final disposition of the matter referred; and in
           particular it may refer a judicial case with request for its
           trial and decision by the higher court.


     3. Define "appeal." How quickly must an appeal be filed?


        a. An appeal is the transfer to a higher court of a judicial case
           on which judgment has been rendered in a lower court, and is
           allowable only to the party against whom the decision has been
           rendered. The parties shall be known as the appellant and
           appellee. An appeal cannot be made to any court other than the
           next higher, except with its consent. Only those who have
           submitted to a regular trial are entitled to an appeal. The
           grounds of appeal are such as the following:
          01. Any irregularity in the proceedings of the lower court
          02. Refusal of reasonable indulgence to a party on trial
          03. Receiving improper or declining to receive proper evidence
          04. Hurrying to a decision before all the testimony is taken
          05. Manifestation of prejudice in the case
          06. Mistake or injustice in the judgment and censure
        b. Written notice of appeal, with supporting reasons, shall be
           filed by the appellant with both the clerk of the lower court
           and the clerk of the higher court, within thirty (30) days
           following the meeting of the court.








     4. Define "complaint." How quickly must a complaint be filed?


        a. A complaint is a written representation made against some act or
           decision of a court of the Church. It is the right of any
           communing member of the Church in good standing to make
           complaint against any action of a court to whose jurisdiction he
           is subject, except that no complaint is allowable in a judicial
           case in which an appeal is pending.
        b. A complaint shall first be made to the court whose act or
           decision is alleged to be in error. Written notice of complaint,
           with supporting reasons, shall be filed with the clerk of the
           court within thirty (30) days following the meeting of the
           court. The court shall consider the complaint at its next stated
           meeting, or at a called meeting prior to its next stated
           meeting. No attempt should be made to circularize the court to
           which complaint is being made by either party.
        c. If, after considering a complaint, the court alleged to be
           delinquent or in error is of the opinion that it has not erred,
           and denies the complaint, the complainant may make complaint to
           the next higher court. If the court fails to consider the
           complaint by or at its next stated meeting, the complainant may
           make complaint to the next higher court. Written notice of
           complaint, together with supporting reasons, shall be filed with
           both the clerk of the lower court and the clerk of the higher
           court within thirty (30) days following the meeting of the lower
           court.


     5. What should happen when a member moves out of the community? What
        should be done when a member neglects the church for a year or
        more? What is an associate member?


        a. When a member moves:
          01. When a member moves out of the community, it shall be his
              duty to transfer his membership by presenting a certificate
              of dismission from the Session of the church of which he is a
              member to the church with which he wishes to unite.
          02. When the church of which he is a member has no Session, or
              for other good reasons it seems impossible for the member to
              secure a certificate of dismission, he may be received by the
              Session upon other satisfactory testimonials, in which case
              the church of which he was a member shall be duly notified.
          03. It shall also be the duty of the teaching and ruling elders
              of the church of which he is a member, as far as possible, to
              continue pastoral oversight of him and to inform him that
              according to the teaching of our Book of Church Order it is
              his duty to transfer his membership as soon as practicable to
              the church in whose bounds he is living.
          04. It shall further be the duty of the church from whose bounds
              the member moved to notify the teaching and ruling elders of
              a church into whose bounds he has moved and request them to
              take pastoral oversight of the member, with a view of having
              him transfer his membership.


        b. Neglect of the church for a year or more:
          01. If a member, after having thus been advised, shall neglect
              for one (1) year to have his membership transferred, the
              Session shall then proceed, according to BCO 38-4 [the member
              shall be warned, if possible, both in person and writing of
              his covenant promises to the church and warn him that if he
              persists his name shall be removed from the roll. If the
              member does not respond, his name shall be erased. However,
              if the member makes a written request for process, the
              Session shall grant such a request], except in special cases
              such as: servicemen, students, etc.


        c. An associate member:
          01. Associate members are those believers temporarily residing in
              a location other than their permanent homes. Such believers
              may become associate members of a particular church without
              ceasing to be communicant members of their home churches. An
              associate member shall have all the rights and privileges of
              that church, with the exception of voting in a congregational
              or corporation meeting, and holding an office in that church.


   P. The Directory for Worship (Chapters 47-63)


     1. What parts of the Directory For Worship have constitutional
        authority (if any)?


        a. The Directory for Worship does not have the force of law and is
           not to be considered obligatory in all its parts. However, BCO
           56 [The Administration of Baptism; The Baptism of Infants and
           Children], 57 [The Admission of Persons to Sealing Ordinances;
           namely, admittance of non-communing members to the Lord's Supper
           after profession of faith and thus a change in status to
           communing members] and 58 [The Administration of the Lord's
           Supper] have been given full constitutional authority by the
           Eleventh General Assembly after being submitted to the
           Presbyteries and receiving the necessary two-thirds (2/3)
           approval of the Presbyteries.


     2. What rule guides public worship? What is the purpose of public
        worship? What are the proper elements of worship? (chapter 47)


        a. Since the Holy Scriptures are the only infallible rule of faith
           and practice, the principles of public worship must be derived
           from the Bible, and from no other source.
        b. The end of public worship is the glory of God. His people should
           engage in all its several parts with an eye single to His glory.
           Public worship has as its aim the building of Christ's Church by
           the perfecting of the saints and the addition to its membership
           of such as are being saved-all to the glory of God.
        c. The Bible teaches that the following are proper elements of the
           worship service:
          01. Reading of Holy Scripture
          02. Singing of Psalms and hymns
          03. Offering of prayer
          04. Preaching of the Word
          05. Presentation of offerings
          06. Confessing the faith
          07. Observing the Sacraments
          08. Taking oaths on special occasions


     3. In brief, how ought we to keep the Lord's Day? (chapter 48)


        a. It is the duty of every person to remember the Lord's Day; and
           to prepare for it before its approach. All worldly business
           should be so ordered, and seasonably laid aside, as that they
           may not be hindered thereby from sanctifying the Sabbath, as the
           Holy Scriptures require.
        b. The whole day is to be kept holy to the Lord; and to be employed
           in the public and private exercises of religion. Therefore, it
           is requisite, that there be a holy resting, all the day, from
           unnecessary labors; and an abstaining from those recreations
           which may be lawful on other days; and also, as much as
           possible, form worldly thoughts and conversation.
        c. Let the provisions for the support of the family on that day be
           so ordered that others be not improperly detained from the
           public worship of God, nor hindered from sanctifying the
           Sabbath.
        d. Let every person and family, in the morning, by secret and
           private prayer, for themselves and others, especially for the
           assistance of God to their minister, and for a blessing upon his
           ministry, by reading the Scriptures, and by holy meditation,
           prepare for communion with God in his public ordinances.
        e. Let the time not used for public worship be spent in prayer, in
           devotional reading, and especially in the study of the
           Scriptures, meditation, catechizing, religious conversation, the
           singing of psalms, hymns, or spiritual songs; visiting the sick,
           relieving the poor, teaching the ignorant, holy resting, and in
           performing such like duties of piety, charity, and mercy.


     4. Who is responsible for deciding who preaches in a church? (chapter
        53)


        a. The Session is responsible for deciding who preaches in a
           church.


     5. What vows do parents make at the baptism of their children?
        (Summarize) (chapter 56)


        a. The vows parents make at the baptism of their children are as
           follows:
          01. Do you acknowledge your child's need of the cleansing blood
              of Jesus Christ, and the renewing grace of the Holy Spirit?
          02. Do you claim God's covenant promises in (his) behalf, and do
              you look in faith to the Lord Jesus Christ for (his)
              salvation, as you do for your own?
          03. Do you now unreservedly dedicate your child to God, and
              promise, in humble reliance upon divine grace, that you will
              endeavor to set before (him) a godly example, that you will
              pray with and for (him), that you will teach (him) the
              doctrines of our holy religion, and that you will strive, by
              all the means of God's appointment, to bring (him) up in the
              nurture and admonition of the Lord?


     6. Who admits people to the Lord's Supper? What vows are made?
        (Chapter 57)


        a. The Session admits people to the Lord's Supper.
        b. The vows made are as follows:
          01. Do you acknowledge yourselves to be sinners in the sight of
              God, justly deserving His displeasure, and without hope save
              in His sovereign mercy?
          02. Do you believe in the Lord Jesus Christ as the Son of God,
              and Savior of sinners, and do you receive and rest upon Him
              alone for salvation as He is offered in the Gospel?
          03. Do you now resolve and promise, in humble reliance upon the
              grace of the Holy Spirit, that you will endeavor to live as
              becomes the followers of Christ?
          04. Do you promise to support the Church in its worship and work
              to the best of your ability?
          05. Do you submit yourselves to the government and discipline of
              the Church, and promise to study its purity and peace?



   Doctrines & Proofs


   Q. The "Five Points" (see below)
     1. Briefly define each of the "five points" and cite two proof texts
        for each (both reference and full quotation). Some texts may
        support more than one point. The following passages may be helpful:
          01. T:    Genesis 6:5; Jeremiah 17:9; Romans 3:10-12; 8:7-8;
              Ephesians 2:1-3
          02. U:    John 6:37, 39; Romans 9:9-13, 16; Ephesians 1:4, 11;
              2:8-10; Titus 3:5
          03. L:    Matthew 1:21; John 6:37, 44; 10:11, 14-16; Romans 8:29-
              30
          04. I:    Ezekiel 36:26-27; John 6:37, 44, 65; 10:16; Acts 11:18;
              13:48; Phil 2:11-13
          05. P: John 6:44; Romans 8:29-30; Phil 1:6


   R. The Ordo Salutis (see above)
     1. List clearly the parts of the ordo as you understand it and cite
        relevant proof texts (both reference and full quotation) that help
        establish the order. The following passages may be helpful:
        a. Romans 8:29-30
        b. Romans 5:1
        c. Romans 6:22
        d. Ephesians 2:8-10
        e. Titus 3:5-7
        f. John 6:37, 39-40, 44
        g. John 10:26-29


   S. Gospel Outline
     1. Simply, briefly and clearly explain the gospel to an unbeliever and
        cite proof texts (both reference and full quotation) for each of
        your main points.
        a. Creation
          01. God, who created all things (Gen 1:1), created men and women
              in his image to be in relationship with him (Gen 1:27).


        b. Fall
          01. That relationship was tragically ruptured when Adam disobeyed
              God's command not to eat from the tree of knowledge of good
              and evil (Gen 2:17) and thus brought death into the world
              (Rom 5:12) and sin, which afflicts us all (Rom 3:23). Thus
              everyone is liable to God's judgment.
        c. Redemption
          01. Ephesians 2:1-10 reiterates that all are afflicted with sin,
              saying that we are spiritually dead and even objects of wrath
              (vv. 1-3). However, through the Gospel, God, because of his
              love and mercy makes his people spiritually alive, raises,
              and seats them with Christ in the heavens to show grace to
              them (vv. 4-7). We are saved by grace through faith, not of
              ourselves, it is the gift of God (vv. 8-9). The way God is
              able to save us is because he imputes our sin to Christ and
              by implication Christ's righteousness to us (2 Cor 5:21).
              Those who are saved become God's workmanship, created to do
              good works which God prepared in advance to do (v. 10). The
              way we become God's workmanship or children (John 1:12) is
              simply to confess and believe that Jesus is "Lord" and that
              God raised him from the dead (Rom 10:9) as pledge that we too
              will be raised from the dead (2 Cor 4:14: "because we know
              that the one who raised the Lord Jesus from the dead will
              also raise us with Jesus....").
        d. Consumation/Judgment
          01. Jesus will return to restore fallen creation (Acts 3:21: "He
              must remain in heaven until the time comes for God to restore
              everything....") and to save his people but he will judge
              those who reject the Gospel (Acts 17:31: "For he has set a
              day when he will judge the world with justice by the man he
              has appointed....").






III. Hot Topics
   A. "Hot Topics" are areas of particular controversy or concern on which
      the candidate should be prepared to briefly state and defend his
      views. In preparing, students should consider the Scriptures, the
      Confession and Catechisms, and Assembly decisions (study papers and
      judicial cases) as recorded in its Minutes. Presbytery's candidates
      committee or stated clerk may be able to offer guidance to relevant
      Assembly actions on these topics. Among the "hot topics" students
      should be prepared to deal with are the following:


     1. Creation
